        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.4c00278"><meta property="og:title" content="One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V1.13Se2/V2O3 Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/acsami.4c00278.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) offer several benefits, including cost-efficiency and fast-charging characteristics, positioning them as attractive substitutes for lithium-ion batteries in energy storage applications. However, the inferior capacity and cycling stability of electrodes in SIBs necessitate further enhancement due to sluggish reaction kinetics. In this respect, the utilization of heterostructures, which can provide an inherent electric field and abundant active sites on the surface, has emerged as a promising strategy for augmenting the cycling stability and rate features of the electrodes. This work delves into the utilization of V1.13Se2/V2O3 heterostructure materials as anodes, initially fabricated via a simplified one-step solid-state sintering technique. The high pseudocapacitance and low characteristic relaxation time constant give the V1.13Se2/V2O3 heterostructure impressive properties, such as a high capacity of 328.5 mAh g–1 even after 1500 cycles at a high current density of 2 A g–1 and rate capability of 278.9 mAh g–1 at 5 A g–1. Moreover, the assembled sodium-ion full battery delivers a capacity of 118.5 mAh g–1 after 1000 cycles at 1 A g–1. These findings provide novel insight and guidance for the rapid synthesis of heterojunction materials and the advancement of SIBs."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/acsami.4c00278.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e67ae982775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e67ae982775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '3b785cce-4451-494e-a30d-b141af13fa0d'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e67ae982775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90f6e67ae982775c-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "One-step Solid-State Synthesis of V&lt;sub&gt;1.13&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;/V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructure as a High Pseudocapacitance Anode for Fast-Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c00278", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

<a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Zhipeng++Sun" data-id="article_author_search">Zhipeng Sun</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D18833%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DXiaofan%2BMa%252C%2BJiangling%2BLuo%252C%2BRui%2BJiang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D15%26contentID%3Dacsami.4c00278%26title%3DOne-step%2BSolid-State%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BV1.13Se2%252FV2O3%2BHeterostructure%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh%2BPseudocapacitance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BFast-Charging%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D18842%26publicationDate%3DApril%2B2024" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0007.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) offer several benefits, including cost-efficiency and fast-charging characteristics, positioning them as attractive substitutes for lithium-ion batteries in energy storage applications. However, the inferior capacity and cycling stability of electrodes in SIBs necessitate further enhancement due to sluggish reaction kinetics. In this respect, the utilization of heterostructures, which can provide an inherent electric field and abundant active sites on the surface, has emerged as a promising strategy for augmenting the cycling stability and rate features of the electrodes. This work delves into the utilization of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure materials as anodes, initially fabricated via a simplified one-step solid-state sintering technique. The high pseudocapacitance and low characteristic relaxation time constant give the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure impressive properties, such as a high capacity of 328.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> even after 1500 cycles at a high current density of 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> and rate capability of 278.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Moreover, the assembled sodium-ion full battery delivers a capacity of 118.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. These findings provide novel insight and guidance for the rapid synthesis of heterojunction materials and the advancement of SIBs.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D18833%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DXiaofan%2BMa%252C%2BJiangling%2BLuo%252C%2BRui%2BJiang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D15%26contentID%3Dacsami.4c00278%26title%3DOne-step%2BSolid-State%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BV1.13Se2%252FV2O3%2BHeterostructure%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh%2BPseudocapacitance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BFast-Charging%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D18842%26publicationDate%3DApril%2B2024" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2024 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Batteries" class="article__tags__link">Batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291484&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Diffraction" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Diffraction" class="article__tags__link">Diffraction</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291338&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrical properties" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrical%20properties" class="article__tags__link">Electrical properties</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291323&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Heterostructures" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Heterostructures" class="article__tags__link">Heterostructures</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode">anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=V1.13se2%2Fv2o3+Heterostructure&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_V1.13Se2%2FV2O3%20heterostructure">V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=One-step+Solid-state+Method&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_one-step%20solid-state%20method">one-step solid-state method</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Lithium-ion batteries, known for their high efficiency and reliability, have become integral in modern life, powering electric cars and portable electronic products. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3" aria-label="reference 1 to 3">(1−3)</a> Despite their widespread use in various commercial fields, further application is limited by the scarcity and high cost of lithium resources. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 4 to 8">(4−8)</a> Compared to lithium, sodium resources are abundant and cost-effective on Earth. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9 ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 9 to 11">(9−11)</a> Therefore, Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted significant attention as a highly anticipated contender for energy storage and transportation applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 12 to 14">(12−14)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">In recent years, layered transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) have garnered extensive concern for their unique physical and chemical properties in the realm of energy storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 15 to 18">(15−18)</a> VSe<sub>2</sub>, a representative member of TMDs, features a large interlayer spacing of 6.11 Å, facilitating Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation. Besides, its metallic properties are conducive to ion storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> However, the lower d-orbital energy level of selenium leads to the reduction of V<sup>4+</sup> and the oxidation of Se<sup>2–</sup>, causing the inherent instability of VSe<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> This instability results in the agglomeration of VSe<sub>2</sub> into bulk materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> Consequently, during the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction processes, VSe<sub>2</sub> experiences substantial volume fluctuations, leading to electrode fragmentation and compromised cycling stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, a nonstoichiometric compound, can be considered a self-intercalating layered material, where excess vanadium is systematically situated amid the continuous Se–V–Se interlayers. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> This unique structure enhances electron transfer efficiency and structural stability throughout repeated cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19 ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref22" aria-label="reference 19 and 22">(19,22)</a> Additionally, the design of heterostructures involving transition metal compounds can achieve coordinated interactions between diverse ions, bringing about remarkable structural stability. For example, Wang et al. reported a V<sub>1.11</sub>S<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/C heterostructure prepared by a multistep reaction process of solvothermal-polymerization-selenylation, delivering excellent rechargeability and durability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> However, the formation of heterostructures with chalcogenide elements (O<sup>2–</sup>, S<sup>2–</sup>, Se<sup>2–</sup>, or Te<sup>2–</sup>) requires an initial bond-breaking process with metal ions, necessitating substantial reaction energy and introducing notable variability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> This complexity has limited the investigation of the synthesis techniques of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and its heterostructures. Consequently, research on V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is scarce, and the synthesis methods are quite complex, highlighting the need for further investigation in this field. It is necessary to seek simple methods to prepare V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and investigate its electrochemical performance.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure was initially synthesized through a convenient one-step solid-state sintering approach. The resulting composite exhibits noteworthy characteristics, including a high specific capacity of 343.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, remarkable rate capability of 278.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, and exceptional cycling performance with a capacity of 328.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 1500 cycles. Moreover, we have explored the storage mechanism of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> by using X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) during the charge–discharge processes. Additionally, the electrochemical behavior of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> as an anode material in full cells has also been comprehensively investigated, revealing its exceptional power storage capabilities.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Synthesis of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub></h3><div class="NLM_p last">V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> was synthesized via a simple solid-state sintering method. Specifically, 70 mg of vanadyl acetylacetonate (C<sub>15</sub>H<sub>24</sub>O<sub>6</sub>V) and 70 mg of selenium were ground together in a mortar and pestled to obtain a homogeneous mixture. The mixture was then heated in a tube furnace under an Ar atmosphere at a heating rate of 5 °C/min to 700 °C and held at this temperature for 3 h. Pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> was synthesized at 700 °C for 1 h with a heating rate of 5 °C/min under an Ar atmosphere using the same synthetic route.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Materials Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The microstructure and morphology of the samples were investigated using scanning electron microscopy (SEM, Hitachi SU8220) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM, Talos F200S, FEI, Thermo). The phase composition and chemical structure of the samples were tested using X-ray diffraction (XRD) with Cu Kα radiation from a Bruker D2 phaser X-ray diffractometer. The surface composition and chemical states were determined using X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, ESCALAB 250xi). Thermogravimetric analysis (TG) was performed in the air and N<sub>2</sub> atmospheres using a synchronized thermal analyzer (409 PC).</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical properties of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> material were tested using a coin-type half-cell. The anode electrode slurry was fabricated by adding active material, carbon black, and sodium carboxymethyl cellulose (CMC-Na) at a weight ratio of 7:2:1 into deionized water and ground thoroughly. The slurry was then uniformly coated on the Cu foil and dried at 60 °C for one night. The mass loading of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> in the electrode was about 1.0–1.2 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. The NaPF<sub>6</sub> (1.0 M) dissolved in diglyme was used as the electrolyte. Charge–discharge tests were performed between 0.01 and 3.0 V on the NEWARE battery test system. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were measured using an electrochemical workstation (CHI 760E). The resistivity of the samples was obtained using a Four-point probe tester (SN/<i>RT</i>S-8).</div><div class="NLM_p last">Using Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as the cathode, 1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in diglyme as the electrolyte, and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> as the anode, a sodium ion full cell was assembled. The cathode electrode slurry was prepared by mixing the active material, carbon black, and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) with a weight ratio of 7:2:1. To balance the capacity between the cathode and anode, the weight ratio between the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@rGO cathode and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> anode was maintained at 3:1. Before the full cell was assembled, the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode was activated for five cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> in the half battery.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a visually demonstrates the successful synthesis of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure by utilizing a straightforward one-step solid-state sintering technique. The surface and morphology characteristics of the heterostructure were analyzed using SEM and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM). In comparison to the distinct block shapes of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>), the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure reveals a blocky morphology with surface-enriched particles as depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b. This unique morphology facilitates efficient interaction between solid and liquid phases, improving the ion transport efficiency. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> HRTEM and selected area electron diffraction (SAED) images confirm the coexistence of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> in the heterostructure (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>c,d). The characteristic lattice spacings of 0.21 and 0.27 nm are evident, corresponding to the (102) plane of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and the (104) plane of V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, respectively. Moreover, a distinct heterointerface between V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is visible, demonstrating atomic matching and rich interface active sites. This heterointerface with abundant interface active sites is beneficial for ion transport. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> Energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>e reveals an even distribution of V, Se, and O elements throughout the structure, further evidencing the successful synthesis of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure. The crystal structure diagram of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>f exhibits a typical layered structure that facilitates Na<sup>+</sup> transport. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> It is worth noting that excess vanadium orderly occupies the interstitial spaces between the consecutive layers of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, increasing the structural stability.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Synthesis route of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, (b) SEM, (c) HRTEM, (d) SAED, and (e) EDS elemental mapping of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, (f) the structure of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The phase structure of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> was determined through XRD analysis in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a. The XRD pattern of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> can be assigned to the hexagonal phases of both V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> (PDF no. 32-1415) and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (PDF no. 34-0187). The refined XRD patterns of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b suggest the coexistence of these two phases (V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>) in the composite material, with a mass ratio of 82:18%. The successful synthesis of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure is additionally supported by the identification of the Se, V, and O elements in the XPS elemental analysis (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>c displays the V 2p spectra of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, revealing doublet peaks at 517.1 and 524.5 eV in V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, attributed to V 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and V 2p<sub>1/2</sub> of V<sup>4+</sup>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 25 and 26">(25,26)</a> respectively. Two additional peaks at 516.0 and 523.5 eV correspond to V 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and V 2p<sub>1/2</sub> of V<sup>3+</sup>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 27 and 28">(27,28)</a> respectively. In Se 3d spectra (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d), the Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and Se 3d<sub>3/2</sub> peaks at approximately 53.0 and 54.0 eV for V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> are assigned to Se<sup>2–</sup>, while the peak at 58.9 eV belongs to Se–O. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30" aria-label="reference 29 and 30">(29,30)</a> Notably, compared to pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, the peaks for V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructures in the V 2p and Se 3d spectra significantly shift toward lower binding energies. These shifts are due to the formation of a heterointerface between V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, indicating the electron transfer between the two materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> This phenomenon can be attributed to the existence of the inherent electric field and the electron coupling interaction between V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 32 and 33">(32,33)</a> Simultaneously, the heterointerface on the surface also partially weakens the further oxidation of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure, explaining the stronger Se–O peak at 58.9 eV for pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> The high-resolution O 1s spectrum of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e) can be resolved into two distinct peaks situated at 530.3 and 532.3 eV, respectively, which correspond to the V–O bond of V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and the absorbed water, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35 ref36" aria-label="reference 35 and 36">(35,36)</a> further corroborating the successful synthesis of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 2</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S3</a> depict the TG curves of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure under air and N<sub>2</sub> atmospheres. The weight of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> gradually increases in the range of 200–320 °C under air, differing from its behavior under an N<sub>2</sub> atmosphere, which can be assigned to the oxidation of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> to V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and SeO<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Moreover, a swift decrease in weight is observed after 320 °C, attributed to the volatilization of SeO<sub>2</sub> as a gaseous byproduct. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> The transformation of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> during the TG testing under air is presented below<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="uneq1"><div class="equation"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mn>2</mn><mn>1.13</mn></mfrac><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi><mn>1.13</mn></msub><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mn>11.39</mn><mn>2.26</mn></mfrac><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">O</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">O</mi><mn>3</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mn>4</mn><mn>1.13</mn></mfrac><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">O</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mstyle></mrow></math></div><div class="label"></div></div></div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) XRD patterns, (b) refined XRD patterns of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, XPS spectra of (c) V 2p, (d) Se 3d, and (e) O 1s, (f) TG curves of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> under air atmosphere.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Theoretical calculations suggest that pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> experiences a weight loss of 73%. The actual weight loss of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is measured at 60%, indicating that the proportion of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> in V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is approximately 87%, closely aligning with the refined XRD results.</div><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical behavior of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure was investigated by using CV at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, as illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a. Upon the initial Na<sup>+</sup> insertion, three cathodic peaks at 0.83, 1.37, and 2.05 V are ascribable to the formation of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>VSe<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>Se. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> On the other hand, distinct anodic peaks at approximately 1.51, 1.84, and 2.06 V are predominantly ascribed to the extraction of Na<sup>+</sup>, the formation of intermediate product Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>VSe<sub>2</sub>, and fully charged product VSe<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5,6)</a> The V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> component in V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> exhibits typical capacitive features with no observable redox peaks, resembling the CV curve of pure V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>). Besides, an initial cathodic peak at 0.36 V vanishes in later cycles, demonstrating the formation of a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref38 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 6, 38 and 39">(6,38,39)</a> The overlapping profiles in subsequent cycles highlight the excellent cycling stability of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b reveals the initial charge–discharge curves of the three electrodes at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Notably, the first charge–discharge curve of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure exhibits some plateaus aligned with the redox peaks observed in CV. The initial charge/discharge capacities for V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> are 422.3/447.7, 411.2/440.8, and 59.2/212.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, yielding initial Coulombic efficiencies of 94, 93, and 28%, respectively. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c presents a comparison of the cycling performances for V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> exhibits a fluctuating capacity with an initial decrease followed by an increase. The initial decrease can be attributed to the formation of an SEI film. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The subsequent increase in capacity is due to further electrolyte penetration into the interior of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> This continuous infiltration enhances the conversion process, resulting in the exposure of more boundary positions and heterogeneous interfaces, consequently enhancing the capacity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> attains the highest capacity of 343.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 50 cycles, with a capacity retention of 96%. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 3</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S5</a> illustrate the rate capability of the three electrodes at various current densities ranging from 0.1 to 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The capacities of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> at these current densities are 374.2, 318.5, 312.6, 306.6, 296.8, and 278.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. When reverting to a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> delivers the highest specific capacity of 366.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a maintenance rate of 98%. On the contrary, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> represent lower capacities of 248.9 and 12.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, highlighting the substantial influence of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> component on the rate performance of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> maintains a capacity of 328.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1500 cycles at a high current density of 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> as displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>e. When the loading mass of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> in the electrode increases to 2–2.5 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>, the electrode can also deliver a capacity of 244.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1200 cycles at the same current density in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>, demonstrating its potential as a high-loading anode material. Conversely, pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> exhibits obvious instability after only 100 cycles, while V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> demonstrates commendable cycling performance but with limited capacity. These results suggest that the advantage of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> over V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> lies in its superior cycling stability. While the capacity of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is mainly contributed by V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, the appearance of the heterostructure confers excellent cycling stability for V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) CV curves of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Charge–discharge profiles at various current densities. (c) Cycling performance at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Rate ability at various current densities. (e) Cycling performance at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To elucidate the disparities in electrochemical performance, the reaction kinetics of the electrode was measured by EIS and CV at different scan rates. The charge transfer resistance (R<sub>ct</sub>) is deduced from the semicircle radius in the Nyquist plot (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a). The V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure exhibits a smaller semicircle diameter in comparison to V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. Precisely, the R<sub>ct</sub> values for the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> are measured as 13.3, 22.5, and 35.3 Ω, respectively, indicating the superior ion conductivity of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure relative to V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. The Bode plots of impedance measurements (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>b and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S7</a>) delineate the real (C′) and imaginary (C″) components of the capacitance for different samples. The real component C′ reflects the contribution of reversible fast electrochemical processes at a given frequency. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> displays a slower decay of C′ with a minimum characteristic relaxation time constant (τ<sub>0</sub>) of 4.2 s, which is much smaller than the values for pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> (7.1 s) and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (14.5 s) as calculated from C″. Besides, the resistivity data in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a> reveal that the resistivity of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is also lower than that of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>. These results demonstrate that the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure exhibits enhanced ion diffusion and transport effects. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a></div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) EIS curves. (b) Bode curves of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. (c) CV curves of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> at different sweep rates. (d) The relationship diagram of peak current and sweep rate. (e) The capacitive controlled portion at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (f) The contribution ratio of capacitance at different sweep rates.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>c, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S4 and S9</a> display the CV curves at different scan rates ranging from 0.1 to 1.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup> to investigate the kinetics behavior of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> electrodes. The relationship between peak current (<i>i</i>) and scan rate (<i>v</i>) can be expressed as <i>i</i> = <i>av</i><sup><i>b</i></sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> The slope value of <i>b</i> can be obtained by fitting the log <i>v</i> and log(<i>i</i>) plots. The <i>b</i> value approaching 0.5 signifies a diffusion-controlled sodium storage process, while the b value near 1 indicates the dominance of surface pseudocapacitance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> As depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S9b</a>, the calculated results reveal that the b values of all peaks for V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> are approximately 1, implying that their sodium storage process is predominantly governed by pseudocapacitance, known for their swift response capabilities. V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure exhibits the highest capacitance fraction with values of 90.8, 92.6, 94.2, 96.2, and 96.7% at scan rates of 0.1, 0.3, 0.5, 0.8, and 1.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>e,f), respectively. This remarkable pseudocapacitive behavior observed in the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode is attributed to its unique heterostructure, which offers additional electrochemical active sites at the heterointerface. The heterointerface promotes interactions between the electrolyte and the electrode, thereby enhancing response kinetics and electrochemical performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Besides, the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode represents a reduction in particle size from 5 to 9 to 3–7 μm as the cycles increase from the initial cycle to 40 cycles shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>, revealing capacity losses in the first few cycles. It is worth mentioning that the electrode’s structure and morphology remain unchanged after 40 cycles, highlighting its remarkable cycle stability.</div><div class="NLM_p">Ex-situ XRD was used to investigate the structural transformation and phase evolution of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, as illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a. During the initial cycle, the peak intensity of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> phase at 29.9° gradually diminishes and subsequently reappears, while the corresponding Na<sub>0.6</sub>VSe<sub>2</sub> (PDF no. 83-1276) phase at 11.8° shows an incremental-then-decremental trend. Besides, at the discharged state, the peak for the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> phase disappears and the peak for Na<sub>2</sub>Se (PDF no. 77-2155) at 23.1° emerges, validating the conversion reaction from V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> to Na<sub>2</sub>Se. In the initial stage, characteristic peaks of the (104) and (110) planes for V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> can be observed at 33.1° and 36.2°, respectively. These peaks exhibit a slight negative shift during the discharging process, indicating that the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> into the V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44 ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 44 and 45">(44,45)</a> The peaks corresponding to Na<sub>2</sub>Se and residual Na<sub>0.6</sub>VSe<sub>2</sub> reappear at the fully discharged state of the second cycle in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b, while the peaks indexed to V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> are observed at the fully charged state, consistent with the products in the initial cycle. Further evidence is provided by HRTEM (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c–f) at cutoff voltages of 0.01 and 3.0 V. The observed lattice spacings of 0.12, 0.19, 0.24, and 0.29 nm correspond to V, Na<sub>2</sub>O, Na<sub>2</sub>Se, and residual Na<sub>0.6</sub>VSe<sub>2</sub> at a discharge potential of 0.01 V, respectively. At the fully charged state (3.0 V), the lattice spacings of 0.26 and 0.36 nm attributed to V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> reappear, along with the heterointerface formed between V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, confirming the generation of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure. These findings demonstrate that the electrochemical reactions involving sodium and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> can be ascribed to the formation of Na<sub>2</sub>O, Na<sub>2</sub>Se, and V during the discharging process, and the regeneration of the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure during the charging process (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>g). The following chemical equations represent the sodium storage mechanism.<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="uneq2"><div class="equation"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle
