class="label"></div></div></div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Ex-situ XRD of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrodes in the (a) initial and (b) second cycles. TEM and SAED images of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> at (c, d) discharged state of 0.01 V and (e, f) charged state of 3.0 V. (g) The phase transformations of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@rGO exhibits high voltage and splendid structural stability as a cathode material for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46" aria-label="reference 46">(46)</a> Hence, a sodium-ion full battery was assembled using Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@rGO as the cathode, NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme as the electrolyte, and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> as the anode to evaluate the practical application of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a. The fully charged battery demonstrates its practicality by effortlessly illuminating 34 commercial light-emitting diodes (LEDs). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b portrays the charge–discharge profiles of the full cell in the initial three cycles, revealing discernible discharging slopes in the voltage range of 1.8–2.5 V, coinciding with the redox peaks in the dQ/dV curve (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>). The full battery delivers average capacities of 170.3, 165.2, 148.4, 128.5, 100.6, and 39.0 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at current densities of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>c, respectively. The capacity can be recovered to 173.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> as the current density decreases from 5 to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, highlighting the impressive rate characteristics. The full battery also demonstrates remarkable cycling stability, maintaining a capacity of 151.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 40 cycles with a capacity conservation rate of 100% in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>d. Furthermore, even after 1000 cycles at a high current density of 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the full cell retains a capacity of 118.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> and a Coulombic efficiency of 100% shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>e. Therefore, the full battery demonstrates competitive electrochemical performance, establishing its potential applications in energy storage.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/medium/am4c00278_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) Schematic illustration of the full cell. (b) Charge–discharge profiles at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Rate ability of the full cell at various current densities from 0.1 to 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Cycling performance at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (e) Cycling performance at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/asset/images/large/am4c00278_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c00278&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">This work focuses on the investigation of a novel anode material, the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure, fabricated through a one-step solid-state sintering method. The heterostructure provides an inherent electric field and abundant active sites on the material surface, thus enhancing performance such as capacity and rate capability. Therefore, the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure shows the highest pseudocapacitance and the lowest characteristic relaxation time constant, indicating fascinating rate capability (278.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>), and remarkable cycling stability (328.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1500 cycles at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>). Similarly, the sodium-ion full battery demonstrates a stable capacity of 118.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> and a high capacity of 170.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Ex-situ technical results manifest a reversible conversion reaction for the V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure during Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction processes. This one-step solid-state sintering method offers a simple and efficient approach for the preparation of similar heterostructure materials.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c00278?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c00278</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">SEM of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>; XPS survey spectrum of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>; TG curve of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> under N<sub>2</sub> atmosphere; CV curves and the capacitive contribution profiles of V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode; charge–discharge profiles of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>, and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> at various current densities; cycling performance of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> with high loading mass; real (C′) and imaginary (C″) components of pure V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>; resistivity of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub> and V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>; CV curves and the capacitive contribution profiles of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>; SEM of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode after different cycles; and dQ/dV curves of V<sub>1.13</sub>Se<sub>2</sub>/V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a></p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c00278/suppl_file/am4c00278_si_001.pdf">am4c00278_si_001.pdf (1.17 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.4c00278" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A low-cost NiSe2 derived from waste nickel foam as a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Lu; Shao, Lianyi; Wang, Shige; Guan, Jieduo; Shi, Xiaoyan; Cai, Junjie; Tarasenko, Nikolai; Sun, Zhipeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">100593</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTPAD5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2542-5293</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel selenide has a splendid future to become a hot anode for sodium ion batteries owing to the high theor. capacity and unique elec. cond.  Nevertheless, exploring low cost and high-performance nickel selenide is still crit. to further application.  Herein, NiSe2 with micro-structured features has been synthesized through a low-cost and one-step selenidation approach using disused nickel foam as raw material.  Eminent reversible capacity (515 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), superior rate capability (310 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and excellent cycling stability (318 mAh g-1 after 800 cycles at 1 A g-1) are exhibited for NiSe2 prepd. at 550 °C for 4 h.  Importantly, the initial Coulombic efficiency is also impressive (96%).  Furthermore, the electrochem. mechanism is sufficiently explored by means of ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  Besides, employing Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO as cathode and NiSe2 as anode has been assembled the sodium ion full battery, which delivers two high discharge plateaus of 1.86 and 2.72 V and reveals preeminent rate capacity and cycling stability.  This work will come out with a new avenue for fostering the evolution of new metal selenide materials for energy storage and others.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-guhKV0gPHrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCcP4c3NRujQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupling of Metallic VSe2 and Conductive Polypyrrole for Boosted Sodium-Ion Storage by Reinforced Conductivity Within and Outside</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Yuhao; Du, Xin; Zhao, Zhipeng; Liu, Yan; Guan, Hui; Liu, Xiaofeng; Pei, Xiangdong; Zhang, Shuo; Li, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although transitional metal dichalcogenides have been regarded as appealing electrodes for sodium/potassium-ion batteries (SIBs/PIBs) owing to their high theor. capacity, it is a key challenge to realize dichalcogenide anodes with long-period cycling performance and high-rate capability because of their poor cond. and large volumetric change.  Herein, polypyrrole-encapsulated VSe2 nanoplates (VSe2@PPy) were prepd. by the selenization of VOOH hollow nanospheres and subsequent in situ polymn. and coating by pyrrole.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In-situ fabrication of active interfaces towards FeSe as advanced performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Shige; Cui, Tingting; Shao, Lianyi; Yang, Shenghong; Yu, Lu; Guan, Jieduo; Shi, Xiaoyan; Cai, Junjie; Sun, Zhipeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal selenides have gained enormous interest as anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Nonetheless, their large vol. expansion causing poor rate and inferior cycle stability during Na+ insertion/extn. process hinders their further applications in SIBs.  Herein, a confined-regulated interfacial engineering strategy towards the synthesis of FeSe microparticles coated by ultrathin nitrogen-doped carbon (NC) is demonstrated (FeSe@NC).  The strong interfacial interaction between FeSe and NC endows FeSe@NC with fast electron/Na+ transport kinetics and outstanding structural stability, delivering unexceptionable rate capability (364 mAh/g at 10 A/g) and preeminent cycling durability (capacity retention of 100% at 1 A/g over 1000 cycles).  Furthermore, various ex situ characterization techniques and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. have been applied to demonstrate the Na+ storage mechanism of FeSe@NC.  The assembled Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO//FeSe@NC full cell also displays a high capacity of 241 mAh/g at 1 A/g with the capacity retention of nearly 100% over 2000 cycles, and delivers a supreme energy d. of 135 Wh kg-1 and a topmost power d. of 495 W kg-1, manifesting the latent applications of FeSe@NC in the fast charging SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqus7eu-EvxwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1BSIfOsmczg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhvFCisrjE&amp;md5=7672184692ae8242048c7d43e7128d2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1093/nsr/nwad118"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Parekh, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rao, A.                 10.1007/s40820-023-01178-3</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D15%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D200%26journal%3DNano-Micro%2BLett.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DX.%2BYi%26author%3DA.%2BM.%2BRao%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DB.%2BLu%26title%3DTrimming%2Bthe%2BDegrees%2Bof%2BFreedom%2Bvia%2Ba%2BK%252B%2BFlux%2BRectifier%2Bfor%2BSafe%2Band%2BLong-Life%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs40820-023-01178-3&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs40820-023-01178-3&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Trimming the Degrees of Freedom via a K+ Flux Rectifier for Safe and Long-Life Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Xianhui; Rao, Apparao M.; Zhou, Jiang; Lu, Bingan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">200</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NLAEBV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2150-5551</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer International Publishing AG</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High degrees of freedom (DOF) for K+ movement in the electrolytes is desirable, because the resulting high ionic cond. helps improve potassium-ion batteries, yet requiring support from highly free and flammable org. solvent mols., seriously affecting battery safety.  Here, we develop a K+ flux rectifier to trim K ion's DOF to 1 and improve electrochem. properties.  Although the ionic cond. is compromised in the K+ flux rectifier, the overall electrochem. performance of PIBs was improved.  An oxidn. stability improvement from 4.0 to 5.9 V was realized, and the formation of dendrites and the dissoln. of org. cathodes were inhibited.  Consequently, the K||K cells continuously cycled over 3,700 h; K||Cu cells operated stably over 800 cycles with the Coulombic efficiency exceeding 99%; and K||graphite cells exhibited high-capacity retention over 74.7% after 1,500 cycles.  Moreover, the 3,4,9,10-perylenetetracarboxylic diimide org. cathodes operated for more than 2,100 cycles and reached year-scale-cycling time.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">VS2 nanoarchitectures assembled by single-crystal nanosheets for enhanced sodium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wenbin; Huang, Jianfeng; Feng, Liangliang; Cao, Liyun; Liu, Yijun; Pan, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">286</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">131-138</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Crystallinity structure plays a key role in the rate capability and cycling performance for rechargeable battery.  However, the effect of crystallinity structure on Na storage properties of VS2 hasn't been clearly elucidated.  VS2 nanoarchitectures comprised of the nanosheets with single-crystal or polycryst. structure are resp. synthesized by a facile solvothermal method, and the influence of crystallinity structure on their Na storage properties is revealed.  The single-crystal structure can largely enhance the Na+ intercalation kinetics in the crystal lattice and the structure stability during charge/discharge process.  Therefore, the single-crystal VS2 electrode exhibits an enhanced rate capability and cycling performance, delivering a high capacity of 193 and 172 mAhg-1 at a high rate of 0.5 and 1.0 Ag-1, and 403 mAhg-1 after the following cycling test of 200 cycles at 0.2 Ag-1.  This work opens up new insights for the exploration and design of high-performance electrode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoUNaqZhiue5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljDh6d56O9QVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsFWjs7%252FP&amp;md5=f623c6351bfe3e50029c4df9a22935a1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.07.036"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nano-Grain Dependent 3D Hierarchical VS<sub>2</sub> Microrods with Enhanced Intercalation Kinetic for Sodium Storage Properties</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-grain dependent 3D hierarchical VS2 microrods with enhanced intercalation kinetic for sodium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wenbin; Huang, Jianfeng; Feng, Liangliang; Cao, Liyun; Liu, Yijun; Pan, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">398</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">91-98</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Construction of well-defined three-dimensional (3D) assembled architectures is an effective strategy to improve the electrochem. reaction kinetics of sodium-ion storage.  Herein, 3D hierarchical VS2 microrods assembled by nanosheets comprised of small VS2 nano-grains are controllably synthesized by a facile in-situ chem. etching approach.  Results show that the addn. amt. of ethanol serving as the etching agent has a great influence on the oriented growth and size (thickness-to-diam. ratio) of VS2 nano-grains.  Moreover, (001)-oriented VS2 nano-grains with larger thickness-to-diam. ratio expose more layer-edges and unsatd. S-edges, and then dramatically improve the intercalation kinetic, eventually leading to the enhancement of rate performance and cycling capacity.  When applied as anode for sodium ion batteries, this material affords a high capacity of 255 and 230 mAhg-1 even at a high rate of 1.0 and 2.0 A g-1, and a reversible capacity of 350 mAhg-1 is still achieved after the following cycling test of 200 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  The controllability and simplicity of the in-situ chem. etching approach, combined with the superior sodium storage properties present a promising strategy for the development of versatile synthesis techniques for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcbVWMeCKoobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljDh6d56O9QVg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solution synthesis of VSe2 nanosheets and their alkali metal ion storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ming, Fangwang; Liang, Hanfeng; Lei, Yongjiu; Zhang, Wenli; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11-16</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Vanadium diselenide (VSe2) is a transition metal dichalcogenide with metallic cond., which makes it a potentially promising electrode material for electrochem. applications.  However, the development of VSe2 electrodes for such applications has been severely hampered by the difficulty of prepg. nanosized products.  In this work, a new facile solvothermal synthesis process is developed and optimized to synthesize ultrathin VSe2 nanosheet assemblies.  To obtain the ultrathin nanosheets, N-Me pyrrolidone, which has similar surface energy to many transition metal dichalcogenides, was used as the solvent to limit the crystal growth along the c-axis direction.  The resulting ultrathin VSe2 nanosheets exhibit good performance toward alk. ion (Li+ and Na+) storage, which can be significantly enhanced by carbon coating.  Specifically, the carbon-coated VSe2 nanosheets can deliver high capacities of 768 mA h g-1 (Li+ storage) and 571 mA h g-1 (Na+ storage) along with outstanding stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvyMbZm4GyDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljDh6d56O9QVg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Influence of interstitial V on structure and properties of ferecrystalline ([SnSe]1.15)1(V1+xSe2)n for n=1, 2, 3, 4, 5, and 6</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Falmbigl, M.; Putzky, D.; Ditto, J.; Johnson, D. C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">231</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">101-107</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JSSCBI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-4596</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ferecryst. compds. ([SnSe]1.15)1(V1+xSe2)n with n = 1-6 and a thin film V1+xSe2 were synthesized using the modulated elemental reactant technique.  The effect of interstitial V-atoms ranging from 0.13≤x≤0.42 in different compds. on structure and elec. properties of these intergrowth compds. is reported.  The presence of the interstitial V-atoms for n&gt;1 was confirmed by Rietveld refinements as well as HAADF-STEM cross sections.  The off-stoichiometry in the thin film V1.13Se2 causes a suppression of the charge d. wave, similar to the effect of nonstoichiometry obsd. for the bulk compd.  The charge d. wave of ([SnSe]1.15)1(V1+xSe2)1, however, is not affected by the nonstoichiometry due to its incorporation as vol. inclusions or due to the quasi 2-dimensionality of the isolated VSe2 layer.  In the compds. ([SnSe]1.15)1(V1+xSe2)n with n = 2-6, the temp. dependence of the elec. resistivity approaches bulk-like behavior.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGopVTQeg4MfYrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQK5bUz3HDBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlyltr%252FP&amp;md5=65fe6c6d2df22477de8026393d739591</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2023.142764"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Woo, H.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polysulfide-derived anion heterogeneous interfaces engineering to facilitate high-efficiency sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jian; Cui, Jing; Li, Zhaojin; Zhang, Di; Sun, Huilan; Wang, Huan; Wang, Qiujun; Woo, H. J.; Ramesh, S.; Wang, Bo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Poor structural stability and inherent low cond. of the transition metal polysulfides often trigger continuous capacity decay.  Here, an anionic heterogeneous modification engineering of the VS4 system is achieved by employing one-step strategy.  The prepd. layered V1.11S2/V1.13Se2/C heterostructure (VSSe/C) exhibits expanded layer distance (5.926 Å) and improved metallicity properties.  Furthermore, the constructed built-in elec. field achieves lower free energy and effective adsorption of reaction products.  Resultantly, when applied to the sodium-ion battery anode, a high specific capacity of 784.9 mA h g-1 is achieved with 500 cycles at a c.d. of 2 A g-1.  Impressively, a high capacity retention of 553.2 mA h g-1 is performed after 1000 cycles at 10 A g-1, which is significantly better than the unmodified VS4 electrode.  Addnl., the assembled sodium ion capacitor exhibits excellent energy densities of 89.1 W h kg-1 at 380 W kg-1 and an ultra-high capacity retention rate of 96.6% over 2000 cycles at a high power d. of 3800 W kg-1.  Ex-situ XRD and XPS results reveal a stable disulfide/selenide conversion process, and no intermediate polysulfide formation.  The design of anionic heterostructures using polysulfide derivs. may provide a ref. for improving the structural properties of anion-rich based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPSfbOKA2yp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQK5bUz3HDBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXnsVymtb4%253D&amp;md5=e7473d102994f90a2fdc52d91505b1e1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsanm.2c00533"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Raj

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heterostructured metallic 1T-VSe2/Ti3C2Tx MXene nanosheets for energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Raj KA, Sree; Mane, Pratap; Radhakrishnan, Sithara; Chakraborty, Brahmananda; Rout, Chandra Sekhar</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Nano Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MXene-based hybrid materials have been expedited extensively for supercapacitors and energy storage applications.  In this work, we have grown the metallic VSe2 layered material on MXene sheets to achieve enhanced energy storage performance.  The VSe2/MXene heterostructures showed improved energy storage performance with a specific capacitance of 144 F/g at a specific current of 1 A/g and a cycling life of 92.8% after 5000 charge-discharge cycles in a two-electrode sym. configuration.  Further, we have presented extensive d. functional theory simulations to study the bonding interaction and electronic properties of VSe2 and its hybrid VSe2/MXene.  The enhanced states near the Fermi level, superior quantum capacitance, and lower diffusion barrier of hybrid VSe2/MXene over the VSe2 support the improved charge storage and better capacitive behavior of the hybrid, as indicated by exptl. observations.  The interaction between VSe2 and the MXene is due to the electronic charge transfer from the Ti 3d orbital of the MXene to V 3d orbital of VSe2, in addn. to weak van der Waals forces.  An asym. supercapacitor was also constructed to exploit the high energy storage performance of the VSe2/MXene electrode.  Further, the VSe2/MXene//MoS2/MWCNT asym. electrode assembly delivered an energy d. of 42 W h/kg at power d. of 2316 W/kg with a capacitance retention of 90% after 5000 charge-discharge cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrC0rdv9T5nqbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQK5bUz3HDBw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Selenium Defect Boosted Electrochemical Performance of Binder-Free VSe2 Nanosheets for Aqueous Zinc-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bai, Youcun; Zhang, Heng; Xiang, Bin; Liang, Xinyue; Hao, Jiangyu; Zhu, Chong; Yan, Lijin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a typical transition-metal dichalcogenides, vanadium diselenide (VSe2) is a promising electrode material for aq. zinc-ion batteries due to its metallic characteristics and excellent electronic cond.  In this work, we propose a strategy of hydrothermal redn. synthesis of stainless-steel (SS)-supported VSe2 nanosheets with defect (VSe2-x-SS), thereby further improving the cond. and activity of VSe2-x-SS.  D. functional theory calcns. confirmed that Se defect can adjust the adsorption energy of Zn2+ ions.  This means that the adsorption/desorption process of Zn2+ ions on VSe2-x-SS is more reversible than that on pure SS-supported VSe2 (VSe2-SS).  As a result, the Zn//VSe2-x-SS battery showed more excellent electrochem. performance than Zn//VSe2-SS.  The VSe2-x-SS electrode shows a good specific capacity of 265.2 mA h g-1 (0.2 A g-1 after 150 cycles), satisfactory rate performance, and impressive cyclic stability.  In addn., we also have explored the energy-storage mechanism of Zn2+ ions in this VSe2-x-SS electrode material.  This study provides an effective strategy for the rational design of electrode materials for electrochem. energy-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxMjL4R0_ZRLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQK5bUz3HDBw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible electrode constructed by encapsulating ultrafine VSe2 in carbon fiber for quasi-solid-state sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Yuanke; Zhong, Wei; Tang, Wenwen; Zhang, Longcheng; Chen, Hao; Li, Qiulin; Xu, Maowen; Bao, Shu-juan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">470</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">228438</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) based on quasi-solid-state electrolyte are a new type of energy device that exhibit high energy and security.  However, the large-vol. expansion and sluggish kinetics of the anode materials during the ion insertion/extn. remains a particular challenge for solid-state SIBs.  In this work, flexible binder-free films composed of ultrafine VSe2 particles wrapped in N-doped carbon nanofibers (VSe2/NCNFs) are prepd. as the anode of a quasi-solid-state SIBs.  The ultra-small VSe2 nanoparticles allow for rapid Na ion migration, and the highly graphitized carbon fibers provides a fast electronic transmission channel and stable host to relive the vol. expansion of VSe2 during cycles.  Foremost, the elastic coordination between VSe2/NCNFs and gel electrolyte can further buffer the overall vol. expansion of VSe2/NCNFs.  Moreover, the flexible freestanding VSe2/NCNFs anode combine with gel polymer in the sodium ion half-cells deliver a high reversible capacity of 420.8 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1, excellent rate capability of 278.1 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1, and 206.8 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 10,000 cycles.  The sodium storage mechanism of VSe2/NCNFs electrodes during the charge/discharge process is also explored by ex situ XRD in the first time.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4n_oDlVyEfbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhskz_ToZ9jmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtFOhsbnN&amp;md5=6ffb4a36f24ff5a9b3981543fd295246</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201809014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jing, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chem-Bonding and Phys-Trapping Se Electrode for Long-Life Rechargeable Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1016/j.jechem.2022.05.025</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D73%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D5-12%26journal%3DJ.%2BEnergy%2BChem.%26author%3DD.%2BGuo%26author%3DM.%2BYuan%26author%3DX.%2BZheng%26author%3DM.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BNan%26author%3DG.%2BSun%26author%3DX.%2BHuang%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26title%3DUltralong%2BCycle%2BLife%2BEnabled%2Bby%2Bin%2BSitu%2BGrowth%2Bof%2BCoMo1%25E2%2580%2593xP%252FMo%2BHeterostructure%2Bfor%2BLithium-Sulfur%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jechem.2022.05.025&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jechem.2022.05.025&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultralong cycle life enabled by in situ growth of CoMo1-xP/Mo heterostructure for lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Donghua; Yuan, Mengwei; Zheng, Xingzi; Li, Miaomiao; Nan, Caiyun; Sun, Genban; Huang, Xianqiang; Li, Huifeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">73</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5-12</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-sulfur batteries (Li-S batteries) are considered as promising new-generation electrochem. energy storage devices due to their extremely high theor. energy d. (2600 Wh kg-1) and theor. specific capacity (1675 mAh g-1).  However, numerous problems such as poor cond. and the shuttle effect during discharge-charge process limit the practical application of lithium-sulfur batteries.  In this work, porous tubular CoMo1-xP/Mo constructed by in situ growth of metal Mo was designed as the sulfur host for lithium-sulfur batteries.  The introduction of Mo modulated the electronic structure of CoMoP to improve the cond. of cathode and facilitate the redox kinetics, as well as the CoMo1-xP/Mo heterostructure was beneficial to inhibit the shuttle effect through the interaction with lithium polysulfides, which improved cycling stability.  As a result, CoMo1-xP/Mo/S cathode had a low-capacity decay rate of only 0.029% per cycle after 2000 cycles at 0.5 C.  This work provided a new perspective for the further design of high-performance lithium-sulfur battery cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0lOJJD0m4_bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhskz_ToZ9jmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFOisLbL&amp;md5=1595b85af5b8a3b94603948750b82f9f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.155156"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ling, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Ordered Macroporous ZnO/ZnS Heterostructure on Carbon Cloth as a Free-Standing Anode with High Areal Capacity for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Alloys Compd.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>835</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">155156</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.155156</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D835%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D155156%26journal%3DJ.%2BAlloys%2BCompd.%26author%3DK.%2BShen%26author%3DS.%2BCai%26author%3DR.%2BLing%26author%3DJ.%2BGuo%26author%3DD.%2BXie%26author%3DJ.%2BSun%26author%3DJ.%2BWei%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26title%3DThree-Dimensional%2BOrdered%2BMacroporous%2BZnO%252FZnS%2BHeterostructure%2Bon%2BCarbon%2BCloth%2Bas%2Ba%2BFree-Standing%2BAnode%2Bwith%2BHigh%2BAreal%2BCapacity%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jallcom.2020.155156&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jallcom.2020.155156&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional ordered macroporous ZnO/ZnS heterostructure on carbon cloth as a free-standing anode with high areal capacity for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Kaier; Cai, Shu; Ling, Rui; Guo, Jinze; Xie, Dongli; Sun, Jiayue; Wei, Jieling; Sun, Xiaohong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">835</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">155156</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0925-8388</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a promising alternative to the Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn intensive attention due to their low cost.  However, the limited areal capacity and cycle life of present sodium anode materials still largely impede their practical application.  In order to obtain an excellent SIBs anode with high areal capacity, the three-dimensional ordered macroporous ZnO/ZnS heterostructure is directly fabricated on carbon cloth (3DOM ZnO/ZnS/CC) via a template method.  From the perspective of materials designing, both the ZnO and ZnS own high specific capacity, meanwhile the ZnO/ZnS heterostructure can low the barrier energy and boost the charge transport.  From the point of electrode engineering, the self-supported 3DOM structure can allow the complete penetration of electrolyte, shorten the ions diffusion path and enlarge the contact area between electrolyte and active materials, which are all beneficial for the mass transfer.  As a result, the as-prepd. electrode delivers a high reversible areal capacity of 1.44 mAh cm-2 at 0.26 mA cm-2 even after 100 cycles.  When elevated to 2.6 mA cm-2, it still maintains at 0.78 mAh cm-2.  This work provides a potential strategy of combining the materials designing and electrode engineering to fabricate the self-supported electrode with high performance for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAYP_3gXj9DbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhskz_ToZ9jmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXosleis78%253D&amp;md5=5e723348b6b42cba4cf912d01ba8c155</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/er.7389"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.                 10.1016/j.electacta.2019.01.076</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D299%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D914-925%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DA.%2BSarkar%26author%3DA.%2BK.%2BSinha%26author%3DS.%2BMitra%26title%3DNanostructured%2Bvanadium%2Btri-oxides%252C%2Bas%2Ba%2Blong%2Blife%2Band%2Bhigh%2Bperformance%2Banode%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbattery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2019.01.076&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2019.01.076&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured vanadium tri-oxides, as a long life and high performance anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sarkar, Ananta; Sinha, Anil Kumar; Mitra, Sagar</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">299</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">914-925</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Choice of hard carbon may not be an ideal selection in rechargeable sodium-ion battery anode when the performance is looked at a higher rate and longer cycle life.  Herein, we report vanadium tri-oxides (V2O3) with different morphol. produced by one step redn. process at a fixed temp. as a power capable sodium-ion battery anode.  The comparison study of these different morphologies of V2O3 electrodes shows the porous hollow nanotube V2O3 electrode display better electrochem. performance against sodium metal in terms of high specific capacity, higher rate capability with extraordinary cycling stability without incorporating any graphene or carbonaceous materials to it.  This porous hollow nanotube exhibits the 2nd cycle reversible capacity of ca. 318 mAh g-1 at a charging rate of 100 mA g-1 and it can even sustain up to 5300 cycles with 90% capacity retention.  The av. Coulombic efficiency was maintained at 99.94% with a very high current rate of 2000 mA g-1.  We further investigate the sodiation mechanism by cyclic voltammetry and XANES technique in details.  The study reveals that with suitable morphol. and appropriate cell design can bring this V2O3 material as a promising anode in future sodium-ion battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpm4f7gskpfQbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhXw8i3hLudpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVenurk%253D&amp;md5=64d2fc5e40fd97cea858cc3ea9f4c4ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1039/D1TA09612E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting Reaction Kinetics and Improving Long Cycle Life in Lamellar VS<sub>2</sub>/MoS<sub>2</sub> Heterojunctions for Superior Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">939</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">949</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D1TA09612E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D939-949%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26issue%3D2%26author%3DR.%2BFan%26author%3DC.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BMa%26author%3DS.%2BLei%26author%3DG.%2BLiang%26author%3DT.%2BHe%26author%3DG.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BCai%26title%3DBoosting%2BReaction%2BKinetics%2Band%2BImproving%2BLong%2BCycle%2BLife%2Bin%2BLamellar%2BVS2%252FMoS2%2BHeterojunctions%2Bfor%2BSuperior%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD1TA09612E&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD1TA09612E&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting reaction kinetics and improving long cycle life in lamellar VS2/MoS2 heterojunctions for superior sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Runze; Zhao, Chenyu; Ma, Jiahui; Lei, Shulai; Liang, Guijie; He, Tao; Zhu, Guocheng; Cai, Yurong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">939-949</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of high-performance rechargeable batteries highly depends on the rational structure/phase design of advanced electrode materials.  A unique 2D lamellar stacked nanosheet VS2/MoS2 heterostructure is synthesized using a simple hydrothermal treatment in this study.  As demonstrated by both exptl. characterizations and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns., the designed VS2/MoS2 heterogeneous composite has multiple structural/compositional advantages as sodium-ion battery anodes, including improved Na+ reaction kinetics, increased Na+ storage capacity, reduced sodiation stress, and a stable solid-electrolyte interface.  Consequently, the VS2/MoS2 heterostructure anode demonstrates excellent comprehensive electrochem. performances, e.g., better initial coulombic efficiency (80.6% at 0.5 A g-1), excellent rate capability (644.0 mA h g-1 at an ultrahigh rate of 10 A g-1), and long cycle life performance (454.5 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1 after 1000 cycles), thus providing more opportunities to realize the high storage capacity and long cycle life of sodium-ion batteries in future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvPbdp2FtQ-bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhXw8i3hLudpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXislyitb3F&amp;md5=825ea785c1d662d4ebda32db62d5774d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2022.154653"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MXene-Derived TiSe<sub>2</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>/C Heterostructured Hexagonal Prisms as High Rate Anodes for Na-Ion and K-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Appl. Eng. Chem. Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>60</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1517</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1525</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.iecr.0c05534</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D60%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D1517-1525%26journal%3DInd.%2BEng.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26issue%3D4%26author%3DH.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BRong%26author%3DZ.%2BYang%26author%3DL.%2BDeng%26author%3DJ.%2BWu%26title%3DV2O3%2540Amorphous%2BCarbon%2Bas%2Ba%2BCathode%2Bof%2BZinc%2BIon%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BHigh%2BStability%2Band%2BLong%2BCycling%2BLife%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.iecr.0c05534&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.iecr.0c05534&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">V2O3@Amorphous Carbon as a Cathode of Zinc Ion Batteries with High Stability and Long Cycling Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Hongzhe; Rong, Yao; Yang, Zhanhong; Deng, Lie; Wu, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Industrial &amp; Engineering Chemistry Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">60</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1517-1525</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IECRED</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0888-5885</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Zinc ion batteries (ZIBs) have the advantages of environmental friendliness, safety, and simple assembly and have strong application potential in the field of energy storage.  In this work, an amorphous carbon-loaded V2O3 (V2O3@AC) material is prepd. by calcination and used as a cathode material for ZIBs.  The V2O3@AC cathode has excellent stability and long life, which maintains 94.8 and 90.7% capacity retention after 180 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 and after 1600 cycles at 1 A g-1, resp.  By SEM (SEM) characterization, V2O3@AC is composed of small irregular nanoparticles, which have a lot of space for electrolyte penetration and ion transmission, and the kinetic studies also confirm this transport capability.  The mechanism of zinc storage is studied by ex situ X-ray powder diffraction, XPS, and SEM technol., and they confirm that V2O3 will undergo phase transition and become V10O24·12H2O during the first charge process.  Due to the high stability and cycle life of V2O3, we believe that it has competitive potential in zinc ion batteries and can play an important role in large-scale energy storage in the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1xMRb3vuhNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhXw8i3hLudpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslOjtr4%253D&amp;md5=105a0b1b59bbcfb7204e9527dc3f848b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202311478"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mechanism of Fast Storage of Li/Na in Complex Sb-Based Hybrid System</span>. <i>Adv.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2023.143738"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F Nanoparticles@reduced Graphene Oxide: A High-Voltage Polyanionic Cathode with Enhanced Reaction Kinetics for Aqueous Zinc-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>468</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">143738</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2023.143738</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D468%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D143738%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DQ.%2BHuang%26author%3DL.%2BShao%26author%3DX.%2BShi%26author%3DJ.%2BGuan%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BWu%26author%3DZ.%2BSun%26title%3DNa3V2O2%2528PO4%25292F%2BNanoparticles%2540reduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%253A%2BA%2BHigh-Voltage%2BPolyanionic%2BCathode%2Bwith%2BEnhanced%2BReaction%2BKinetics%2Bfor%2BAqueous%2BZinc-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2023.143738&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c00278&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2023.143738&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanoparticles@reduced graphene oxide: a high-voltage polyanionic cathode with enhanced reaction kinetics for aqueous zinc-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Qiaofeng; Shao, Lianyi; Shi, Xiaoyan; Guan, Jieduo; Xu, Junling; Wu, Yanxue; Sun, Zhipeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">468</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">143738</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2O2(PO4)2F is characterized by a high theor. specific capacity, high-voltage plateaus, large ion diffusion channels, and stable three-dimensional structure, which is a promising cathode candidate for rechargeable aq. zinc-ion batteries (AZIBs).  Nevertheless, the low electronic cond. hinders its cycling and rate performance.  In this work, a facile microwave-assisted solvothermal approach with postheat treatment has successfully produced Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanoparticles with the dimension of 20-50nm wrapped by reduced graphene oxide (rGO).  The high-pseudocapacitive contribution/diffusion coeff., low electrochem. impedance, favorable electrode wettability, and stable structure can be obtained by optimizing the chem. components of electrolyte and the content of rGO, facilitating the Zn2+ storage performance.  Hence, Na3V2O2(PO4)2F@rGO delivers excellent electrochem. properties such as a high capacity of 127.0 mAh g-1 at 0.5C, a stable capacity of 63.9 mAh g-1 at 30C after 5000 cycles, and a high av. voltage plateau of 1.50 V in hybrid aq. electrolyte (2M zinc trifluoromethane sulfonate (Zn(OTf)2) and 4M lithium trifluoromethane sulfonate (LiOTf)).  Furthermore, exceptional cycling performance in the soft-pack batteries with the size of 3 x 3.5 cm2 includes a reversible capacity of 84.1 mAh g-1 at 10C after 1000 cycles.  In situ X-ray diffraction, ex situ XPS, transmission electron microscopy, and SEM reveal reversible Zn2+ insertion/extn. process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmNDe5-0H8IrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhXw8i3hLudpA"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1016/j.mtphys.2021.100593</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A low-cost NiSe2 derived from waste nickel foam as a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Lu; Shao, Lianyi; Wang, Shige; Guan, Jieduo; Shi, Xiaoyan; Cai, Junjie; Tarasenko, Nikolai; Sun, Zhipeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">100593</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTPAD5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2542-5293</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel selenide has a splendid future to become a hot anode for sodium ion batteries owing to the high theor. capacity and unique elec. cond.  Nevertheless, exploring low cost and high-performance nickel selenide is still crit. to further application.  Herein, NiSe2 with micro-structured features has been synthesized through a low-cost and one-step selenidation approach using disused nickel foam as raw material.  Eminent reversible capacity (515 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), superior rate capability (310 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and excellent cycling stability (318 mAh g-1 after 800 cycles at 1 A g-1) are exhibited for NiSe2 prepd. at 550 °C for 4 h.  Importantly, the initial Coulombic efficiency is also impressive (96%).  Furthermore, the electrochem. mechanism is sufficiently explored by means of ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  Besides, employing Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO as cathode and NiSe2 as anode has been assembled the sodium ion full battery, which delivers two high discharge plateaus of 1.86 and 2.72 V and reveals preeminent rate capacity and cycling stability.  This work will come out with a new avenue for fostering the evolution of new metal selenide materials for energy storage and others.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-guhKV0gPHrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh_vP5agevrSA"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsnano.2c00169</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupling of Metallic VSe2 and Conductive Polypyrrole for Boosted Sodium-Ion Storage by Reinforced Conductivity Within and Outside</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Yuhao; Du, Xin; Zhao, Zhipeng; Liu, Yan; Guan, Hui; Liu, Xiaofeng; Pei, Xiangdong; Zhang, Shuo; Li, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7772-7782</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although transitional metal dichalcogenides have been regarded as appealing electrodes for sodium/potassium-ion batteries (SIBs/PIBs) owing to their high theor. capacity, it is a key challenge to realize dichalcogenide anodes with long-period cycling performance and high-rate capability because of their poor cond. and large volumetric change.  Herein, polypyrrole-encapsulated VSe2 nanoplates (VSe2@PPy) were prepd. by the selenization of VOOH hollow nanospheres and subsequent in situ polymn. and coating by pyrrole.  Benefiting from the inherent metallicity of VSe2, the improvement in the cond. and the structural protection provided by the PPy layer, the VSe2@PPy nanoplates exhibited enhanced sodium/potassium-storage performances, delivering a superior rate capability with a capacity of 260.0 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1 in SIBs and 148.6 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1 in PIBs, as well as revealing an ultrastability in cycling of 324.6 mA h g-1 after 2800 cycles at 4 A g-1 in SIBs.  Moreover, the insertion and conversion mechanisms of VSe2@PPy in SIBs with intermediates of Na0.6VSe2, NaVSe2, and VSe were elucidated by in situ/ex situ X-ray diffraction combined with ex situ transmission electron microscopy observation and in situ potentio-electrochem. impedance spectroscopy during the sodiation and desodiation processes.  D. functional theory calcns. show that the strong coupling between VSe2 and PPy not only causes it to have a stronger total d. of states and a built-in elec. field, leading to an increased elec. cond., but also effectively decreases the ion diffusion barrier.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrlXKUXvH7Xb7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limL0aJsGhFOg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtVaiur3O&amp;md5=3a1b13695170ed64ee9276d489f10595</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1039/C9QI00809H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Rough Endoplasmic Reticulum-like VSe<sub>2</sub>/rGO Anode for Superior Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Inorg.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal selenides have gained enormous interest as anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs). Herein, a confined-regulated interfacial engineering strategy towards the synthesis of FeSe microparticles coated by ultrathin nitrogen-doped carbon (NC) is demonstrated (FeSe@NC).  The strong interfacial interaction between FeSe and NC endows FeSe@NC with fast electron/Na+ transport kinetics and outstanding structural stability, delivering unexceptionable rate capability (364 mAh/g at 10 A/g) and preeminent cycling durability (capacity retention of 100% at 1 A/g over 1000 cycles).         </div><div class="casAbstract">High degrees of freedom (DOF) for K+ movement in the electrolytes is desirable, because the resulting high ionic cond. helps improve potassium-ion batteries, yet requiring support from highly free and flammable org. solvent mols., seriously affecting battery safety.  Here, we develop a K+ flux rectifier to trim K ion's DOF to 1 and improve electrochem. properties.  Although the ionic cond. is compromised in the K+ flux rectifier, the overall electrochem. performance of PIBs was improved.  An oxidn. stability improvement from 4.0 to 5.9 V was realized, and the formation of dendrites and the dissoln. of org. cathodes were inhibited.  Consequently, the K||K cells continuously cycled over 3,700 h; K||Cu cells operated stably over 800 cycles with the Coulombic efficiency exceeding 99%; and K||graphite cells exhibited high-capacity retention over 74.7% after 1,500 cycles.  Moreover, the 3,4,9,10-perylenetetracarboxylic diimide org. cathodes operated for more than 2,100 cycles and reached year-scale-cycling time.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Crystallinity structure plays a key role in the rate capability and cycling performance for rechargeable battery.  However, the effect of crystallinity structure on Na storage properties of VS2 hasn't been clearly elucidated.  VS2 nanoarchitectures comprised of the nanosheets with single-crystal or polycryst. structure are resp. synthesized by a facile solvothermal method, and the influence of crystallinity structure on their Na storage properties is revealed. However, the development of VSe2 electrodes for such applications has been severely hampered by the difficulty of prepg. nanosized products.  In this work, a new facile solvothermal synthesis process is developed and optimized to synthesize ultrathin VSe2 nanosheet assemblies.  To obtain the ultrathin nanosheets, N-Me pyrrolidone, which has similar surface energy to many transition metal dichalcogenides, was used as the solvent to limit the crystal growth along the c-axis direction.
